<div id="review_78730393" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="Jimmy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2742865-jimmy"><img alt="Jimmy" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/m_50x66-82093808bca726cb3249a493fbd3bd0f.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/78730393?book_show_action=true">Nov 23, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jimmy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jimmy" href="/user/show/2742865-jimmy">Jimmy</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer78730393" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17340238282956870076">	This gripping book by Nancy Farmer is about a boy who is a little farmer brat that is given the chance of a lifetime and takes advantage of it. Jack is taught to be a bard by Dragon Tongue and is and taken on life threatening adventures.<br/><br/>	 The bard of their town named Dragon Tongue is an all powerful wizard who takes Jack under his wing and teaches him the ways of a bard. When the Northman King finds out about Dragon Tonguesâ€™ existence he sends a nightmare to take the bardsâ€™ wits. The northmen c</span>
  <span id="freeText17340238282956870076" style="display:none">	This gripping book by Nancy Farmer is about a boy who is a little farmer brat that is given the chance of a lifetime and takes advantage of it. Jack is taught to be a bard by Dragon Tongue and is and taken on life threatening adventures.<br /><br />	 The bard of their town named Dragon Tongue is an all powerful wizard who takes Jack under his wing and teaches him the ways of a bard. When the Northman King finds out about Dragon Tonguesâ€™ existence he sends a nightmare to take the bardsâ€™ wits. The northmen come and Jack and his sister Lucy are taken prisoner and go on crazy adventures; such as raiding a town and slaughtering everyone, fighting a troll-bear, killing dragons and much more. The writing style of this book is gripping and makes the reader want to start on the next book as soon youâ€™re done. The adventures they go on are so far outside of reality that it makes you wonder how life would be if you could actually do these things.<br /><br />	This three time newbery honor author has written The Sea of Trolls as the book of our time. Once I got into the book it pulled me in and glued my face to the pages as I whipped through them. This book is great for anyone who likes magic, â€œfantasy likeâ€ creatures and concepts, or if you are just looking for an amazing read. This book offers the same reading experience that the Harry Potter series has and more.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17340238282956870076" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_233000631" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/233000631" />
    <a title="Evan Hays" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3365907-evan-hays"><img alt="Evan Hays" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1267543842p2/3365907.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/233000631?book_show_action=true">Nov 08, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Evan Hays" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Evan Hays" href="/user/show/3365907-evan-hays">Evan Hays</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3365907-evan-hays?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3365907-evan-hays?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer233000631" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9301911759233220045">The best children's/young adult book I have read since the Graveyard Book. Highly recommend this one. The author, who actually has a science background, really did her historical research for this one. The backdrop is northeastern England (probably somewhere around what today would be Newcastle) around the year 800 AD. This is Saxon England, England greatly influenced by Celtic Christianity, England that still holds onto many of its pre-Christian ideas and mythology, and England on the verge of </span>
  <span id="freeText9301911759233220045" style="display:none">The best children's/young adult book I have read since the Graveyard Book. Highly recommend this one. The author, who actually has a science background, really did her historical research for this one. The backdrop is northeastern England (probably somewhere around what today would be Newcastle) around the year 800 AD. This is Saxon England, England greatly influenced by Celtic Christianity, England that still holds onto many of its pre-Christian ideas and mythology, and England on the verge of Viking raids. How can you not love that? <br /><br />Not the best writing I have ever read, but you do get into the characters and she does a good job of describing the setting for the most part. The real strength of the story I would say is that things are never simple. We always see the good and the bad side of people. For example, by the end of the story, the main character Jack sees the Northmen as some of his closest friends even though he had seen them murder and pillage and had been taken by them as a thrall. So much for that, but the important part is that the author portrays Jack, who has a full knowledge of both sides of the Northmen, learning to live in tension with those divergent versions of the Northmen. This is excellent, because this is what it is like to really live in the real world.<br /><br />I am onto the second one of this trilogy already.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9301911759233220045" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_550666011" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/550666011" />
    <a title="Kelley Ceccato" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3176174-kelley-ceccato"><img alt="Kelley Ceccato" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/550666011?book_show_action=true">Mar 02, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kelley Ceccato" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kelley Ceccato" href="/user/show/3176174-kelley-ceccato">Kelley Ceccato</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3176174-kelley-ceccato?shelf=far-from-feminist">far-from-feminist</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer550666011" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17258877057062507612">This is a rollicking adventure, a feast if you like Norse mythology. I have to admit I was thoroughly entertained by this book, even as I spent a good bit of it grinding my teeth. I would recommend this to any young boy who loves fantasy and adventure -- but I would hesitate before suggesting it to any girl who loves same.<br/><br/>The book's main flaw, and it's a big one (for me, anyway), is that its female characters are uniformly repellent. Of all of them, only the very minor characters of Heide and (p</span>
  <span id="freeText17258877057062507612" style="display:none">This is a rollicking adventure, a feast if you like Norse mythology. I have to admit I was thoroughly entertained by this book, even as I spent a good bit of it grinding my teeth. I would recommend this to any young boy who loves fantasy and adventure -- but I would hesitate before suggesting it to any girl who loves same.<br /><br />The book's main flaw, and it's a big one (for me, anyway), is that its female characters are uniformly repellent. Of all of them, only the very minor characters of Heide and (possibly) Jack's mother are sympathetic. All of the major evil, dangerous, and/or untrustworthy monsters -- dragon, trolls, half-troll Queen -- are female, and the two main human females are no better: Lucy is the sort of brat one itches to drown, and Thorgil is a girl-warrior for readers who hate girl-warriors. It's almost as if Farmer is endorsing the "girls have cooties" ethos of the supposed male target demographic, and leaving little or nothing that girls could latch onto. If a man had written the book, I'd suspect he was either a raving misogynist or had decided misogynistic tendencies.<br /><br />It's a shame, because there's so much to like about this book. </span>
  <a data-text-id="17258877057062507612" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_298627394" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/298627394" />
    <a title="Janessa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/947145-janessa"><img alt="Janessa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1262582446p2/947145.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/298627394?book_show_action=true">Mar 21, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Janessa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Janessa" href="/user/show/947145-janessa">Janessa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/947145-janessa?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer298627394" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1009820519321270873">I loved this book the first time I read it, years ago, and loved it even more reading it the second time with my fifth grader. The setting is beautifully realized - the primitive northern villages of the Vikings, the early Anglo-Saxon settlements, and the icy mountains of Jotunheim. The cast of characters is diverse, vivid, heroic, humorous, and frightening. Jack's quest to free his younger sister, Lucy, from the Troll Queen after Lucy is captured by Vikings is compelling and completely engaged </span>
  <span id="freeText1009820519321270873" style="display:none">I loved this book the first time I read it, years ago, and loved it even more reading it the second time with my fifth grader. The setting is beautifully realized - the primitive northern villages of the Vikings, the early Anglo-Saxon settlements, and the icy mountains of Jotunheim. The cast of characters is diverse, vivid, heroic, humorous, and frightening. Jack's quest to free his younger sister, Lucy, from the Troll Queen after Lucy is captured by Vikings is compelling and completely engaged my son. At times it is violent, but other moments are tender. It was fun to hear my son chuckle at the idiosyncrasies of characters like the feisty shield maiden, Thorgill, or at Jack's sharp sense of irony. Reading this book sent my son on a search through books about Viking Mythology, much like reading the Percy Jackson series interested him in Greek Mythology. We both thoroughly enjoyed it. </span>
  <a data-text-id="1009820519321270873" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('jGYZ2YYSYlkkOOMRnxaj80wkd9DCAnLQqSlzh9s2PEVf8ai+DeHqCB017L/nMInEAOfauA2hTzOPbyUaKst+dg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('fcXePNqVBnL69RkoCYeRK9wjrA/Vh7ePHZIbeHXy7MCuUm9bUWaOI8P4FoZxobsckOABZxokimw71E3lhA+u8w==')})
  }

The town has 4,500 residents and the high school arena seats 7,000.           <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer4222986797265084140">Nancy was born in 1941 in Phoenix and grew up in a hotel on the Arizona-Mexico border where she worked the switchboard at the age of nine. She also found time to hang out in the old state prison and the hobo jungle along the banks of the Colorado River. She attended Reed College in Portland, Oregon, earning her BA in 1963. Instead of taking a regular job, she joined the Peace Corps and was sent to</span>
  <span id="freeText4222986797265084140" style="display:none">Nancy was born in 1941 in Phoenix and grew up in a hotel on the Arizona-Mexico border where she worked the switchboard at the age of nine. She also found time to hang out in the old state prison and the hobo jungle along the banks of the Colorado River. She attended Reed College in Portland, Oregon, earning her BA in 1963. Instead of taking a regular job, she joined the Peace Corps and was sent to India (1963-1965). When she returned, she moved into a commune in Berkeley, sold newspapers on the street for a while, then got a job in the Entomology department at UC Berkeley and also took courses in Chemistry there. Restless, again, she decided to visit Africa. She and a friend tried to hitchhike by boat but the ship they'd selected turned out to be stolen and was boarded by the Coast Guard just outside the Golden Gate Bridge. Nancy eventually got to Africa on a legal ship. She spent more than a year on Lake Cabora Bassa in Mozambique, monitoring water weeds. Next she was hired to help control tsetse fly in the dense bush on the banks of the Zambezi in Zimbabwe. Part of the time she spent in the capital, Harare, and was introduced to her soon-to-be husband by his soon-to-be ex-girlfriend. He proposed a week later. Harold and Nancy now live in the Chiricahua Mountains of Arizona on a major drug route for the Sinaloa Cartel. This is the setting for The Lord of Opium. They have a son, Daniel, who is in the U.S. navy.<br /> Nancy's honors include the National Book Award for The House of the Scorpion and Newbery Honors for The Ear, the Eye and The Arm, A Girl Named Disaster and The House of the Scorpion. She is the author of nine novels, three picture books and a number of short stories. Her books have been translated into 26 languages.<br /><br /></span>

This partial loads on almost every page view.  The associated React component makes
a call to SignInPromptController#get to determine if the user should see the sign in interstial.
This is determined by how many signed out pagehits the user has executed an how recently they have
last seen the insterstitial.  If the controller responds indicating the popup should appear, the
